  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d1929d53-62e1-4d16-8d94-100833795a56'

              <span id="reviewTextContainer242826265" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8518390949389621652"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1438596613p8/1217599.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a href='https://just0nemorepage.tumblr.com/post/623472309944172544/into-the-cold-fire-lynne-ewing-daughters-of' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>This review is also posted on my blog.</b>
</a><br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[So I’m not sure what it is about these books – they’re not without their problems, and they’re a bit too simple even for their intended age range, and they didn’t particularly age the best – but I still have a soft spot for them. I devoured the whole series in middle school and I LOVED it then, and re-reading it now in my late 20’s-early 30’s, I still enjoy them quite a bit.<br/><br/>And I DEFINITELY can see how this helped spark my love of the aest</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8518390949389621652" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1438596613p8/1217599.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://just0nemorepage.tumblr.com/post/623472309944172544/into-the-cold-fire-lynne-ewing-daughters-of" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>This review is also posted on my blog.</b>
</a><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So I’m not sure what it is about these books – they’re not without their problems, and they’re a bit too simple even for their intended age range, and they didn’t particularly age the best – but I still have a soft spot for them. I devoured the whole series in middle school and I LOVED it then, and re-reading it now in my late 20’s-early 30’s, I still enjoy them quite a bit.<br><br>And I DEFINITELY can see how this helped spark my love of the aesthetic, good lord.<br><br>But it’s the issues I mentioned that drop it down to three stars, cause augh they can’t be overlooked. The lack of offensive power on the Daughters’ parts, the dependence on stereotypes, the obvious plot twists, the boy-craziness, how adult and sexualized *15-year-old girls* are portrayed, how wolf whistles and catcalls and any sort of sexual male attention is painted as a good thing… just, generally there’s quite a bit wrong with it, but the overall story and plot driving things in the background is still keeping me going. It still feels just like the first book did - good underlying plot and story, but mostly still disappointing. I’m not sure whether or not I’d recommend the series to anybody who wouldn’t be able to read it with a grain of salt, frankly. But if you can.. if you’re able to read things and think of them critically, then give it a try, if it interests you. This still definitely has that Sailor Moon magical girl feel to it.<br><br>And Jimena holding Serena in the fire in order to save her as she slowly dies herself got to me a bit. (Though she was also revived a little too easily… but maybe sometimes I like simple revives. It wears a lot less on my stress level LOL.)<br><br>I don’t have too much else to say about it, really. This felt very similar to the first book, as I already said, and I already said everything that needed to be said in my review of it. I feel like I’d just be repreating myself here, so if you’re curious, go read that review!<br><br>Sooner or later, on to the third book.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_827010401" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827010401" />
    <a title="Veronica Morfi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5510829-veronica-morfi"><img alt="Veronica Morfi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419153500p2/5510829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827010401?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica Morfi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica Morfi" href="/user/show/5510829-veronica-morfi">Veronica Morfi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827010401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4939504379064200359">Rating: 3/5<br/><br/>Into the Cold Fire is the second book the the Daughters of the Moon series and it focuses around Serena, the Daughter with the power to read minds. Just like in the first book I loved the interactions of all four girls but I wasn't the biggest fan of Serena (my favorite is still Catty and I can't wait for her book). <br/><br/>In this book Serena is being targeted by the Atrox to join his army. I really enjoy getting to know more about the Atrox and the Followers. Serena is being pulled closer t</span>
  <span id="freeText4939504379064200359" style="display:none">Rating: 3/5<br /><br />Into the Cold Fire is the second book the the Daughters of the Moon series and it focuses around Serena, the Daughter with the power to read minds. Just like in the first book I loved the interactions of all four girls but I wasn't the biggest fan of Serena (my favorite is still Catty and I can't wait for her book). <br /><br />In this book Serena is being targeted by the Atrox to join his army. I really enjoy getting to know more about the Atrox and the Followers. Serena is being pulled closer to the darkness and has no idea how she will get out of it. Until the end I didn't know in which side she would end up.<br /><br />The one thing I adored about this book, just like the first one, is the dark, bad guy, Stanton. I loved the scenes with him and Serena, but since Serena had some memory gaps, I missed all the parts she didn't remember. And it was so frustrating that we never got to see those parts. It would have been so cute seeing those two together.<br /><br />I also enjoyed the relationship between Jimena, the daughter who can see the future, and Collin, Serena's brother. Those two fight all the time but you can still feel the tension between is more than it originally looks like. The next book is Jimena's, so I can't wait to see if she and Collin would be a thing.<br /><br />All in all, the second book had the exact same tone as the first one. Funny, fast-paced, some action and quite a few cute moments. I am really looking forward to reading the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4939504379064200359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1399665278490568416" style="display:none">This fun adventure takes you through the lives of teenage girls as they navigate through the troubles of boys, school, and romance. <span id="freeTextContainer17597397093887772376">For starters, I think I enjoyed this book much more than the first one. This book focuses on Serena, who is probably my favorite of the four girls. As a result I connected more to this book than the first.<br/><br/>GOOD: As i said, i like this book much more than the first.   <span id="freeText17597397093887772376" style="display:none">For starters, I think I enjoyed this book much more than the first one. This book focuses on Serena, who is probably my favorite of the four girls. As a result I connected more to this book than the first.<br /><br />GOOD: As i said, i like this book much more than the first. I connected really well with Serena, so it made the book that much more enjoyable. I like the plot of this one more as well! Every detail seemed to connect so well and it all resolved into a great ending. I cant wait to move on to the third book!<br /><br />BAD: One major thing bothered me about this book. It's not nessesarly a big deal, but it got a bit on my nerves. That thing is that she kept asking her self questions purposely to build suspense or to create foreshadowing. This isn't bad when done once or twice, but it's done multiple times in practically every chapter! Again, it's not technically bad, but once I realized it was happening it was hard to NOT wait for it to happen again. Besides that, there honestly wasnt much else wrong. Good plot, good writing (besides what i just mentioned), the rest is good to me!<br /><br />I cant wait for the third book! I'm really excited to see a plot in Jimena's eyes! I'm also excited to see if it beats the second book. 4 stars for Into the Cold Fire!<br /><br />TRIGGER WARNINGS: I cant really think of any besides brief satanic(?) Like I said, I feel like I'm rating these from the first time I read them when I was 15 and not now, BUT that being said, Serena is my bitch and I love her. She's my favorite Goddess for such. We get a different main character for every book but at the same time, all the same characters. A different story, just the same main arc. It's pretty awesome.<br /><br /><br />Maybe Spoilers? I don't know.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I also loved all the side characters and thought they were perfect for the age group. Cassandra and Morgan make good villains, Zahi made a good villain. And don't get me STARTED on Stanton. Yeah, it might be way YA this book, but that forbidden romance is there, and I LOVE it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3149097456684268817"><i>CHECKED OUT THE BOOK FROM MY PUBLIC LIBRARY.<br/><br/>APART OF THE GOODREADS 2011 READING CHALLENGE.<br/><br/>2ND REVIEW. 1ST REVIEW IS <a href='http://iceprincessreviews.wordpress.com/2010/01/05/into-the-cold-fire-by-lynne-ewing/' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>.<br/><br/><u>Review/Rating:</u><br/><br/>5 out of 5</i><br/><br/>Serena’s power to read minds comes in handy sometimes, but it also makes her more at risk to turning to the Atrox. So, when the Atrox attempts to turn her, what will the rest of the Daughters of the Moon do?   <span id="freeText3149097456684268817" style="display:none"><i>CHECKED OUT THE BOOK FROM MY PUBLIC LIBRARY.<br /><br />APART OF THE GOODREADS 2011 READING CHALLENGE.<br /><br />2ND REVIEW. 1ST REVIEW IS <a href="http://iceprincessreviews.wordpress.com/2010/01/05/into-the-cold-fire-by-lynne-ewing/" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.<br /><br /><u>Review/Rating:</u><br /><br />5 out of 5</i><br /><br />Serena’s power to read minds comes in handy sometimes, but it also makes her more at risk to turning to the Atrox. So, when the Atrox attempts to turn her, what will the rest of the Daughters of the Moon do? Will Jimena and the rest of the Daughters be able to prevent the premonition of Serena turning?<br /><br />I decided to do a better review of the Daughters of the Moon series by Lynne Ewing since my first ones weren’t done very well. This book is really a fast read. I finished it in a week, but that’s only because I had to go to work. &gt;.&lt;<br /><br />In the second book of this series, it explains about Hekate and how she is a Goddess of the Night, and also how she might be credited to evil. Also, there are 13 books in this series, so more information about the Daughters of the Moon and the Atrox will show up as the books progress, which is a good thing because it isn’t cramped all into one book.<br /><br />The tone and dialogue reminds me a lot of my teenage years and my high school, so the author did a really good job at writing the book in teenage words and their world. The descriptions were also very well done, and both of these things made the book go a little bit faster than most other young adult books. So, I really like this book from this stand point. Another thing I liked about this book is the mythology that is incorporated in it. Also, the character growth and their personalities are believable (for a supernatural book). I can’t wait until I re-read the next book in this series. This book starts out better than the first one since you have a little bit more information to go on. Also, my favorite character is Stanton. :) Yes, I'm weird and like all types of guys from different kinds of books.<br /><br />The plot isn’t that much different from other supernatural books or shows since it is basically teenage girls fighting evil, which might remind some people of Sailor Moon and several other anime. That might be way I like it since it kind of reminds me of most of the anime I watch. Oh, well, I like that and mythology so it was perfect book for me. Also, there is a little bit more, errr, sexual tension than the first book.<br /><br />Any more information would spoil this book and series. :D I can't wait to start on the next book in the series (again).</span>

<div id="review_533333214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533333214" />
    <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness"><img alt="Paranormal_Madness" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468451974p2/17012067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533333214?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paranormal_Madness" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness">Paranormal_Madness</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533333214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3776136168169259080"><b>What I liked:</b><br/>-Serena and Jimena’s friendship. They’re very close—more like sisters than just friends—and it really shows in this book. Jimena is willing to risk her own life just to save Serena, and I absolutely love friendships like that.<br/>-Secondary cast. Catty is probably my favorite of the four girls, and Vanessa is a close second, but I also like Jimena and Maggie and Stanton. Unfortunately with this book, I found myself enjoying the parts about the other girls instead of Serena’s problems.<br/>-S</span>
  <span id="freeText3776136168169259080" style="display:none"><b>What I liked:</b><br />-Serena and Jimena’s friendship. They’re very close—more like sisters than just friends—and it really shows in this book. Jimena is willing to risk her own life just to save Serena, and I absolutely love friendships like that.<br />-Secondary cast. Catty is probably my favorite of the four girls, and Vanessa is a close second, but I also like Jimena and Maggie and Stanton. Unfortunately with this book, I found myself enjoying the parts about the other girls instead of Serena’s problems.<br />-Stanton. He’s one of my favorite things about this series. I like how his character always keeps you guessing, and you can never truly tell where his loyalties lie, because he’ll do anything to survive, even possibly abandoning the girls in their time of need. He’s dark, mysterious, and sexy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Way too sexy for Serena. He belongs with Vanessa. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>What I disliked:</b><br />-Writing. It felt very juvenile, and even though I’m older than the target audience, I should have still been able to enjoy the writing, but I didn’t. It was very choppy and it didn’t flow very well, and it lacked description of any kind.<br />-Length. These books are very short, and the writing is larger than average and so is the spacing, so that makes them even shorter than they appear. They probably could have been either lengthened out or she could have made them parts and put more than one together.<br />-Serena. I’m not sure why, but I’m not a huge fan of Serena, and the books that center around her are my least favorite of the series. I just never connected with her like I did the other girls.<br /><br />Overall, this is one of my lesser favorites from the series, but the plot is good and it kept me interested. If you liked the first one and you like Serena, you’ll definitely like this book as well. <b>2.5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3776136168169259080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15535008906184641398">This is the second book in the Daughters of the Moon series, and Serena is the narrator of this book. <br/>Her talent is the ability to read minds, where her best friend Jimena gets premonitions of the future.   <span id="freeText15535008906184641398" style="display:none">This is the second book in the Daughters of the Moon series, and Serena is the narrator of this book. <br />Her talent is the ability to read minds, where her best friend Jimena gets premonitions of the future. Their mentor Maggie has helped them hone, or understand their skills. Serena is a bit of a rebel, and doesn't always follow the rules, and she is in danger as Stanton, the sexy leader of Atrox's Followers, is after her to subvert her powers towards evil to bring the Daughters of Moon down.<br /><br />Serena has a tough time in this one, as her friend Jimena does get a premonition about Serena that has her friends not trusting her. I like her surfer brother Collin, though he has no clue that his sister is so different. Her powers are strongest when the moon is fullest, and the Followers powers are strongest at the dark of the moon. They have the ability to get into your mind and make you want to join them.<br /><br />Serena meets a new boy at school that she likes, and he is from another country. Since his thoughts are in another language, she might actually be able to finally have a normal relationship... But there's a bit of conflict where Stanton is trying to warn her away from this guy. Serena gets some conflicting signals, and she doesn't know who to trust, and it's hard to confide in friends who don't seem to trust you.<br /><br />I really felt for Serena, but I didn't feel as connected to the story and characters as I was the first novel. Still held my interest, but I'm not sure I plan on reading the entire series. </span>

  <span id="freeText10330732969786576173" style="display:none"> This story is about four girls with extraordinary abilities. Serena who has the ability to read minds, Jimena who has premonitions, Catty who can skip back and forth through time, and Vanessa who can turn invisible. In this book Serena is the one more focused on. Serena runs into trouble when the Atrox, an evil force set out to destroy the girls, happens to be at the beach where Serena and her brother are surfing. There she sees a fire, interested she walks towards it to find that it’s freezing, frightened she runs and falls off the cliff to the sand below. What happens next? Read the book!<br /> <br /> I could totally relate to Jimena. Her free spirit reminds me of what I am like on the weekends. When I was reading I could feel all the emotions in the book. The breath each took, the fear trembling off their skin. It was amazing.<br /> <br /> I absolutely love this book. My favorite part of the book was towards the end. Serena got caught in the fire and Jimena ran into save her even if it meant risking her life. That friendship is just phenomenal, risking your life to save another. There wasn’t a single part in the book I didn't like. This book was fantastic.<br /> <br /> I would definitely recommend this book to a friend. Most likely to a girl because it's more of a chick flick type of book than an action book. I would recommend this book to anyone interested in fairytale sort of books. Read the series it's amazing!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382685513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1594543591958994783">I definitely was more invested in this novel than the first, because I felt like I got to know the girls better in this one. I like Serena more than I liked Vanessa, and I can't wait to read Jimena's POV novel, because she seems awesome.<br/><br/>Serena, Jimena, Catty, and Vanessa are all best friends now, and they are working on controlling their powers together. Serena spends a night at the beach with her brother and sees an evil Atrox initiation ritual involving a cold fire that makes you immortal, but</span>
  <span id="freeText1594543591958994783" style="display:none">I definitely was more invested in this novel than the first, because I felt like I got to know the girls better in this one. I like Serena more than I liked Vanessa, and I can't wait to read Jimena's POV novel, because she seems awesome.<br /><br />Serena, Jimena, Catty, and Vanessa are all best friends now, and they are working on controlling their powers together. Serena spends a night at the beach with her brother and sees an evil Atrox initiation ritual involving a cold fire that makes you immortal, but a slave to the Atrox. She passes it off as a dream and starts seeing a cute Moroccan student named Zahi, who can speak French and Arabic and thinks in those languages, which makes it easy for mind-reading Serena to be around him. But Maggie and the other girls don't trust Zahi, and a cryptic taroh reading and a scary premonition from Jimena only confirm their suspicions that Zahi is not who them think he is. <br /><br />This was a great, diverse, girl-power YA novel. It is a good fantasy novel for young girls that also shows real youth culture that involves gangs, partying, and drug-taking while still portraying young people as smart, strong, and brave. The writing is sometimes cheesy and dated, and you know it is written by an older woman trying hard to know what the kids are into these days, but Ewing gets an A for effort. At least she's writing novels that challenge young readers and she gives them characters who are diverse and colorful.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer111577547&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer111577547" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14730428672019446666">This is the second time I've read this book. The first time was about a decade ago when I was in junior high school. It is really amazing how much you forget about a book that you read so long ago. I really loved the book then and I find I still love it now. I guess that shows whether a book stands the test of time. This is the second book in the Daughters of the Moon series and is told from the point of view of Serena who has the gift of telepathy. She also seems to have an affinity for the dar</span>
  <span id="freeText14730428672019446666" style="display:none">This is the second time I've read this book. The first time was about a decade ago when I was in junior high school. It is really amazing how much you forget about a book that you read so long ago. I really loved the book then and I find I still love it now. I guess that shows whether a book stands the test of time. This is the second book in the Daughters of the Moon series and is told from the point of view of Serena who has the gift of telepathy. She also seems to have an affinity for the dark side of the moon and the goddess Hekate. Now most people would think she was evil but as the book tells us Hekate was given the bad rap because she always escorted Persephone on her trips to the underworld. In this book Serena is under the thrall of Zahi a Follower who is trying to get Serena to step into the cold fire, an entity that will strip her of her humanity. Along the way another Follower, Stanton, seems to generally want to help her. Overall, I am extremely excited to re-read this series and to find out all the things I missed before.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14730428672019446666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192016468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12112321696815880456">Hm... This book had an interesting idea, but I think the twists were all given away because I vaguely recalled having read it so many years ago when I was in high school. I don't know if I would have felt differently about it if I hadn't known - for the most part - what was going to happen.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[For instance, I knew that Zahi was a Follower which I think was cool. I knew that Stanton and Serena were a couple, too, but I want to know how that even happened, so it's a little frustrating j</span></span>
  <span id="freeText12112321696815880456" style="display:none">Hm... This book had an interesting idea, but I think the twists were all given away because I vaguely recalled having read it so many years ago when I was in high school. I don't know if I would have felt differently about it if I hadn't known - for the most part - what was going to happen.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For instance, I knew that Zahi was a Follower which I think was cool. I knew that Stanton and Serena were a couple, too, but I want to know how that even happened, so it's a little frustrating just... not knowing. It feels like I'm missing part of the story even though the order in which the author wrote it was creative and interesting.<br /><br />Also, I wish that Serena had been a Follower for longer than what... two pages? I think it could have been an extremely interesting dynamic to have the Goddesses have to deal with their friend and find a way to turn her back against her will.<br /><br />It was cool to see that Jimena was willing to sacrifice her life to save her friend, though.<br /><br />All in all, just an okay book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

Serena panics and runs over to help the girl but when her skin comes in contact with the flames she is surprised to find that the flames are cold. Then she realized this is not any kind of party but that she has run into a group of followers of the Atrox. The Atrox is evil and he wants to kill all the daughters of the moon, and he only has more power to do that when the daughters are most vulnerable. The day/night of the dark moon.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DPN6mrFT4clbND67unCdVBwnAaA7SFtm5VJkSHEUyYDBetpsp3iqCdwUgcLduqBN+w7BTmZs7bAWHHvrv1ApCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mnDKnGR+0dqtXUCT8nsYk2gqVl00kzAL0qxGxN6avcdX+WpqclWaGip9/+qVsSWKjwOWs2m3ht0h4llnEN5dTA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12177491912374305575">Lynne Ewing is an American author and a screen writer.<br/><br/>She always had to move around a lot when she was growing up because her father was in the Marine Corps. She has two sisters. Lynne graduated from high school in Lima, Peru after attending seven other schools. While she was in Peru, she learned to speak Spanish. She attended the University of California at Santa Barbara. When she was 30 years ol</span>
  <span id="freeText12177491912374305575" style="display:none">Lynne Ewing is an American author and a screen writer.<br /><br />She always had to move around a lot when she was growing up because her father was in the Marine Corps. She has two sisters. Lynne graduated from high school in Lima, Peru after attending seven other schools. While she was in Peru, she learned to speak Spanish. She attended the University of California at Santa Barbara. When she was 30 years old, she began writing for newspapers, documentaries, magazines, and did screen writing. She also counsels troubled teens. Her first books were Drive-By and Party Girl. Drive-By took six years to write, and Party Girl has been made into a movie called Living the Life. She has written the completed Daughters of the Moon and Sons of the Dark series. She lives in Los Angeles and Washington D.C.. Ms. Ewing has two children, Jonathan, a molecular biologist, and Amber, an international lawyer. She has also traveled to Japan, China, Russia, Europe, Malaysia, Singapore, Laos, Myanmar, and Thailand. She has begun a new series called Sisters of Isis.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12177491912374305575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
